# Dashboard PRD Plan: Pulse Surfaces

**Source:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md`
**Generated:** 2026-04-25
**Source hash:** `d8d6577a02262ae354afc897f3f3cb132a22be06d135861e2b8c6fa87bb5612d`
**Section tasks:** 53
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/status.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/projections.rs`
- `crates/roko-runtime/src/heartbeat.rs`

### DASH-11-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:7` through `23`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

The Pulse section answers the question: "What is happening?" It is the heartbeat display of the Nunchi dashboard. Users arrive at Pulse when they want to see real-time activity — their agents, the network, the flow of events.

Pulse is the default landing section for users with active agents. The Command Center is the first page most users see on login. It is also where users return when they want a quick read on state without drilling into a specific object.

Pulse contains four pages: Command Center, Live Console, Event Stream, Network Pulse. Each serves a different level of abstraction:

- **Command Center** — high-level aggregate: network-wide KPIs, chain intelligence, what my fleet is doing.
- **Live Console** — one-row-per-agent detail: every agent I have access to, in a dense table.
- **Event Stream** — the raw feed: every typed event, filterable, pausable.
- **Network Pulse** — global-lens view: activity across the whole network, zoomed out.

All four pages are live. All four update continuously via WebSocket subscriptions (see `10-realtime-and-motion.md`). All four apply reactive aesthetics (see `08-epistemic-aesthetics.md`) where appropriate.

---
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `184`
- Section hash: `db1eb95f1f9fb2edb24727ceac2ba7a2bb5e48b5c7ea7f7c9b89d164abfa2813`

**Normative requirements and implementation claims:**
- The Pulse section answers the question: "What is happening?" It is the heartbeat display of the Nunchi dashboard. Users arrive at Pulse when they want to see real-time activity — their agents, the network, the flow of events.
- Pulse is the default landing section for users with active agents. The Command Center is the first page most users see on login. It is also where users return when they want a quick read on state without drilling into a specific object.
- Pulse contains four pages: Command Center, Live Console, Event Stream, Network Pulse. Each serves a different level of abstraction:
- - **Command Center** — high-level aggregate: network-wide KPIs, chain intelligence, what my fleet is doing. - **Live Console** — one-row-per-agent detail: every agent I have access to, in a dense table. - **Event Stream** — the raw feed: every typed event, filterable, pausable. - **Network Pulse** — global-lens view: activity across the whole network, zoomed out.
- All four pages are live. All four update continuously via WebSocket subscriptions (see `10-realtime-and-motion.md`). All four apply reactive aesthetics (see `08-epistemic-aesthetics.md`) where appropriate.
- ---

### DASH-11-S007 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:39` through `84`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `auth`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

Top to bottom, the page has four sections. Each section has a numbered marker, a serif title, an italic description, and the content itself. This follows the pattern already present in the existing dashboard and is retained.

**Header area** (persistent, across all Pulse pages): page title "Command Center," block height indicator on the right with LIVE/CALM status, current lens switcher pill group.

**Section 01 — Live Pulse.** Description: "Real-time chain state, fleet census, and collective intelligence. Every block carries forward what agents learned."

Content: a large banner card showing the current chain state. The banner has:

- A "BLK MIRAGE DEVNET" (or "BLK KORAI MAINNET" in production) label at top-left.
- The current block height as a hero value in mono, large typography.
- A small buffer indicator showing blocks buffered and approximate block rate.
- A horizontal row of recent block pills showing the last 10-15 blocks with animated progression.

Below the banner, a 5-KPI row of hero KPI cards (per `09-visualization-primitives.md`):

- **Block Height** — current block, live ticking.
- **On-Chain Agents** — count of registered agents in scope.
- **ISFR Rate** — current ISFR value, with small trajectory indicator.
- **Knowledge Entries** — count of knowledge entries in scope.
- **Pheromones** — count of active pheromones in scope.

Each KPI card uses the reactive live-number-glyph effect — brief brightening on update. KPIs update continuously via their relevant subscriptions.

**Section 02 — Chain Intelligence.** Description: "The collective mind. Knowledge propagates, pheromones decay, agents converge toward shared understanding."

Content: a three-column layout, each column a composed panel.

- **Left panel — Knowledge Layer.** Compact list of the most recent or most-active knowledge entries (5-8 visible). Each entry shows type tag (insight/warning/heuristic), author agent, short preview, confidence bar, freshness indicator. Users can scroll within the panel. A search input at the bottom. Click an entry to navigate to Entry Detail.
- **Middle panel — Stigmergy Field.** A compact rendering of the Stigmergy Field primitive (`09-visualization-primitives.md`), scaled down. Shows active pheromones. A summary row beneath shows counts by type (wisdom N, opportunity M, threat K). Click the field to navigate to Knowledge → Stigmergy.
- **Right panel — Agent Collective.** A compact list of agents in scope showing their status, recent activity, and tier badge. Summary row beneath: total N, online M, offline K, insights produced J, tasks completed P. Click an agent to navigate to Agent Detail.

**Section 03 — Active Work.** Description: "Jobs in flight, plans executing, bounties at stake."

Content: a two-column layout.

- **Left panel — Running Jobs.** Each active job shown as a compact card: job type, agent assigned, progress bar, estimated completion, current status.
- **Right panel — Executing Plans.** Each running plan shown as a compact card: plan name, step progress (N of M complete), current step summary, time elapsed.

Both panels have "View all" links to their full surfaces (Jobs page in System, Plans page in Forge).

**Section 04 — Market Signals.** *(optional, appears only for users who have engaged with Treasury / trading)*

Content: ISFR curve, recent clearing outcomes, position summary. Data summarized; drill-down via "View Treasury" link.
````

### DASH-11-S009 -- Reactivity hooks

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:94` through `102`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- KPI values use the live-number-glyph ticking effect.
- Block pills have heartbeat rhythm (subtle pulse per new block).
- Knowledge Layer entries show epistemic glow for high-sharpness entries.
- Stigmergy Field uses its full reactivity (particle density, decay fade, type colors).
- Agent Collective entries show heartbeat rhythm per agent's tick cadence.
- High-importance events in Active Work (job completed, plan stuck) flash briefly on arrival.
````

- Storage: define deterministic schema, migration/default behavior, corruption handling, restart recovery, cleanup/GC, and fixture data.
- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.
- Knowledge/learning: preserve provenance, confidence, lineage, decay, retrieval, promotion/demotion, episode signals, and queryable outputs.

### DASH-11-S018 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:146` through `164`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Live Console," block height, lens switcher. Additional: a summary line showing agent counts ("N agents, M online, K plans, uptime").

**Section 01 — Live Console.** Description: "The mixing board. Every agent, every heartbeat, one view."

Content: a table using the Live Console Rows primitive (`09-visualization-primitives.md`). Columns:

- **Agent** — generative portrait, name, short ID.
- **Model** — the model the agent is configured to use.
- **Domain / Task** — domain tag, current task summary.
- **Gate %** — pass rate across recent gates.
- **Cost** — current tick cost or rate.
- **Freq** — current tick frequency (last tick time, cadence indicator).

Each row is live: heartbeat rhythm on status dot, cost updates as events come in, gate % updates as gates fire.

Filter controls above the table: search by name/ID, filter by domain, filter by status, filter by tier, group by domain.
````

### DASH-11-S020 -- Reactivity hooks

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:171` through `178`

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- Each row has heartbeat rhythm matched to the agent's actual heartbeat.
- Velocity streaks on rapidly-changing gate %.
- Muted opacity on paused or idle agents.
- Error state tint (subtle `--error` overlay) on failing rows.
- Generative portraits use their own reactivity (glow tied to activity).
````

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click a row → Agent Detail.

- Right-click a row → context menu: Message, Pause, Abort, View Replay, View Passport.
- Bulk select via checkboxes → bulk actions (pause all, message all).
- Sort columns by clicking headers.
````

- Storage: define deterministic schema, migration/default behavior, corruption handling, restart recovery, cleanup/GC, and fixture data.
- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-11-S029 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:221` through `244`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Event Stream," block height, lens switcher. Additional summary: event count, signal count, WS connection status.

**Section 01 — Event Stream.** Description: "Every signal, every heartbeat, every pheromone deposit. The raw feed."

Content:

- **Filter bar** (top of section). Contains:
  - **Type filter**: dropdown of event types (or "All types").
  - **Search input**: full-text search over event payloads.
  - **Pause button**: freezes the stream.
  - **Export button**: download shown events as JSON or CSV.
  - **Shown count**: "N shown" indicating how many events are in the filtered view.

- **Event list** (fills the rest of the page). Uses the Event Stream Entry primitive. Each row:
  - Timestamp (mono, greyed).
  - Event type tag (caps, colored by type family).
  - Agent ID (if applicable, as a link).
  - Payload preview (mono, truncated; full on click).
  - Severity tint for warning/error events.

- **Status bar** at the bottom: "N events, M signals, WS: connected" or similar.
````

- - **Pause button**: freezes the stream.
- - **Export button**: download shown events as JSON or CSV.
- - **Shown count**: "N shown" indicating how many events are in the filtered view.
- - **Event list** (fills the rest of the page). Uses the Event Stream Entry primitive. Each row:
- - Timestamp (mono, greyed).
- - Event type tag (caps, colored by type family).
- - Agent ID (if applicable, as a link).
- - Payload preview (mono, truncated; full on click).
- - Severity tint for warning/error events.
- - **Status bar** at the bottom: "N events, M signals, WS: connected" or similar.

### DASH-11-S031 -- Reactivity hooks

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:250` through `257`
**Heading level:** H3

**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Reactivity hooks

- New events fade in softly on arrival (per standard appearance pattern).
- Event type tags glow briefly (200ms) on arrival.
- Older events slightly fade as they age (recency-driven opacity reduction).
- Severity colors applied to row accent (warn yellow, error red).
- When paused, the stream visibly freezes and a "PAUSED" banner appears.
````

**Explicit detail extraction from this section:**

- Section word count: `51`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click an event row → expand inline to show full payload.
- Double-click → navigate to the agent or object referenced in the event.
- Filter and search are live — applied as the user types.
- Pause/resume toggles streaming.
- Export produces a file containing the currently-filtered events over a user-chosen time range.
- Keyboard shortcuts: `/` to focus search, `p` to toggle pause, `e` to export.
````

### DASH-11-S040 -- Page structure

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:300` through `340`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `verification`, `config-deployment`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Network Pulse," chain indicator, lens switcher.

**Section 01 — Network Census.** Description: "The collective as a whole. Every agent, every domain, every knowledge layer."

Content: a row of hero KPIs showing network-wide totals:

- Total registered agents (all tiers).
- Total knowledge entries published.
- Total active pheromones.
- Total arenas.
- Total published evals.
- Network-wide 24h episode count.

**Section 02 — Activity Heatmap.** Description: "Where activity concentrates across the network."

Content: a visualization showing network activity distributed across domains. Options: a density treemap where each domain is a rectangle sized by recent activity; or a radial chart with domains arrayed around a center. The visualization refreshes live — activity "breathes" as new events arrive.

Drill-down: click a domain region to filter the rest of the page to that domain.

**Section 03 — Flow Patterns.** Description: "Knowledge and pheromones moving through the collective."

Content: a composite visualization showing cross-domain knowledge and pheromone flows. Specifically:

- A simplified Resonance Graph at network scale, showing cross-domain bridges.
- An animated overlay showing knowledge-retrieval and pheromone-decay events as small flows between domains.

**Section 04 — Cohort Activity.** Description: "How reputation cohorts are engaging."

Content: a breakdown of network activity by reputation tier. Shows:

- What percentage of recent activity is from each tier.
- Which tier is producing the most knowledge.
- Which tier is validating the most.
- Which tier is bringing the most novel content.

**Section 05 — Recent Network Milestones.** Description: "Notable events across the collective."

Content: a curated feed of network-level events: new Sovereign-tier agents, significant leaderboard changes, highly-validated new knowledge, arena concluded with upsets, novel meta-agents produced.
````

- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-11-S048 -- Defaults

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/11-pulse-surfaces.md:380` through `384`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Defaults

- New users with no agents land on the Command Center in Fleet Lens (showing zero-state with clear CTAs to create their first agent) or, alternatively, on Network Pulse in Global Lens to see what the system looks like. This is a design choice; the default is configurable per user in Settings.
- Users with agents land on Command Center in Fleet Lens by default.
````

### DASH-11-S052 -- Offline and stale handling

````markdown
### Offline and stale handling

When subscriptions disconnect, the LIVE indicator becomes STALE. KPI values retain their last known value but show a subtle stale indicator. On reconnect, CATCHING UP appears briefly, then LIVE resumes. See `10-realtime-and-motion.md` for full behavior.
````
